< review>
Let me give you the real scoop on this bike shop.  First, they know what they're doing. So don't be hesitant about the services rendered.  And they carry some decent brands that you wouldn't see at your traditional bike shop.  That being said, the owner is just a cranky dood.  Similarly to what others have said in previous reviews, the guy is just Mr. Grumpipants. He has no idea how to treat customers.  And this message is for his son who also works in the shop:  "Your dad is murdering the business reputation!  You need to either stick him in the back of the shop away from the customers, or open up your own store.  Because that guy is the true barrier from the store being successful.  Trust me!"   I went in there to get a basic part for my bike.  I used to race bmx competitively, so I know my way around fixing it myself.  I decided to pick up the part late, like 7:00 PM, removed a few parts out front of the shop so I could replace the part that was broken.  And keep in mind the shop is located in a semi-ghetto area.  We aren't talking free valet parking here. I needed to borrow 2 tools and I got reprimanded how they don't let people work on bikes in the parking lot.  And that they don't lend out tools.  Begrudgingly they did lend me the tools, which I was ever so grateful, but the attitude was just uncalled for.  It's unbelievable that shops like this can carry this type of attitude.  Seeing how they are all closing their shops not being able to compete with the big box stores or even the online vendors.  The only thing that's keeping good shops alive is great service and the promotion of a biking community that can depend on shops like this to do it right for local customers.  This means not enforcing stupid rules about parking lot quick fixes for paying customers.   It just blows my mind how these business owners think they can run their business while maintaining a healthy return customer base.  Bottom line is.... don't be a dick and your bottom line will increase.<//review>

A kind of romantic, rustic ambiance with plants all around and twinkle lights. The bread came freshly baked in a flower pot and the butter was deliciously light/very whipped with twinges of sage and thyme. The menu featured a nice array of healthy options, and, at least the harvest bowl, was just as delicious as it sounded and with all its components perfectly cooked. On the fancier end, it‚Äôs in a nice in between spot, where it‚Äôs not casual but not the super fancy restaurant you need to make reservations for well in advance. Perfect for a romantic date or birthday celebration.< /review>

<gmap_id>0x808fbb35ad88d2b7:0xc3a9b539eaf3118<//gmap_id>< Rating>

< review>
Walking into Terrain is quite the pleasant experience! The ambiance and decor gives you an earthy feeling with a touch of luxury. Once you're seated, you're attended to quickly and they bring the most delicious bread that's been baked in a terracotta type pot. The scallion butter intensifies the taste of the bread and I would visit this place again just to taste the mix. Though the menu choices are quite limited (only reason for the 4-star rating), menu items are delicious and wholesome as they use ingredients from local farms. The sweet drop pepper on the salmon toast was the perfect combo and accompanied the mushroom soup well. Though Terrain has ample seating, it is not a noisy place unlike other around the mall restaurants. They also have a bar and a large wine menu. Highly recommend!<//review>

< text>
A really fine little place on the edge of Stanford Shopping Center. Especially good for breakfast and lunch. You see all kinds here--- parents with strollers, business lunches, Anthropologie shoppers and more. Nice vibe. There's plenty of room at the counter if the place is busy, and they have a couple of long tables for team meals. Outdoor seating, too, but it's on the hot side of the building with lots of direct sun so be careful. Menu includes breakfast all day, and the omelettes are wonderful. Nice selection of fresh salads. Great salmon. Amazing hummus board starter. Very respectable burger and fries. Hot homemade bread served in little tin pots.  Affordable wine list and some original non alcoholic drinks like fresh juice spritzers. Lunch for three today without drinks was $90, which included one starter and three mains.<//text>

<Text>Smart Millennial style decor (farmhouse/barn style) and menu in Stanford shopping center. The menu is limited (not many items), and the food quality is competent but uninspired. The food materials are high quality. This is a good place for a quick bite or a group to enjoy a meal together. The interior can be noisy at peak times. <user>108889683836617327584<//user><pictures>None</pictures><Resp>None<//Resp><review>Extremely disappointing. For a restaurant that was billed as 4.5 stars by Open Table and Google Maps, and one with pretensions to being "exceptional" with a > $120/couple dinner (without alcohol) that featured artful description of dishes, Terrain really didn't measure. The cooking was OK, but the design of their dishes was... amateurish: every dish!

1. Roasted-apple, fennel & arugula salad: with a weird combo of too-crunchy all-arugula (I felt like a horse chomping) greens & tooth-sticking cubes of carmelized oat & seeds (what is that??), this salad fell very short. Odd extremes of bits of foods made the mouth-feel really strange, and ultimately unsatisfying. Roasted apple was the only saving grace, but not enough to save the dish.

2. Charcuterie:  A big dish - definitely not an "appetizer" and priced accordingly at $22... very ordinary and uninteresting hard crostini. Cheese was good, pate was fine, but the salami was just weird.

3. Scallops: Wow $30 for 3 little scallops? They tasted very fishy, and there was sand in the scallops. I was prompted to ask whether the scallops were fresh or frozen. When told they were "fresh", I concluded these must have been held-over stock in a refrigerator. I know what FRESH scallops taste like, and they do not taste like ones I ate! Only thing good was the squash sauce. Again, really unsatisfying.

4. Striped Bass: Fish was at least fresh and appropriately prepared. Nothing particularly wrong with the dish but there was no flavor to the dish at all. Unmemorable.

I'd say the only that impressed was the fresh bread. But for the price and expectations set by the restaurant, this was a real miss!<//review>< rate>

< review>
I've been to Terrain on few occasions at different days of the week and times of the day: beware they have a very limited menu in the mid afternoon, between lunch and dinner. The menu changes seasonally and I haven't come across a dish I don't like, but some are better prepared than others. The soups are creamy, love the kale Cesar salad and the Brussels sprouts, the scallops is a nice dish, but my zucchini were overcooked, while the 3 scallops in the dish were not evenly cooked, and IMO too much mayo was used for decorating. Teas are nice, mango Margarita is tasty, but barely felt the alcohol. I do enjoy the ambiance of the place with fresh flowers and plants, the bread served in a flower pot, but service is inconsistent, e.g. on Sunday evening, ~7 with almost empty room, our server checked on us just once, brought the bread after our food order and upon our request, then let us wait for the check on an empty table. Also pricey for the type of establishment the Terrain Cafe is.</review>

Allison S<//name>
< Text>
I've dined here off and on since Terrain opened last year. Last November it was an ok experience. Things have improved greatly since then (new management, servers becoming more experienced, new chef) but my mall dining rules are basically in the off hours only so if I'm there on the weekend and it was brunch, it's a 10am sort of thing. If I'm there during the week, it's 11 or 2. I hate crowds and I hate waiting, so that's just how I roll. The only exception to this rule of mine is if I have made reservations.

I happened to be at the mall yesterday so I wanted to grab a light bite to eat. The salmon toast was excellent, and compared to the crab toast it has definitely gotten easier to eat in terms of the bread. This was easily bitten into, and I could also cut it with my butter knife.

The potted bread with cardamom butter is still delicious.

I had chamomile tea but the teapots are a little weird, definitely let it steep a long time before you pour. The mesh basket doesn't seem to go far enough into the teapot to really let everything mingle.

I'll be back for sure.</Text>

< text>
Worst Chipotle I ever visited on 8/06/16, and I've been to many throughout LA. Ordered a quesadilla and it barely had any meat. It was beef which costs the most like $8. Might as well have ordered a burrito and could've actually had enough to eat. Cashier told me I had to cut my quesadilla. How the F am I going to cut it myself? A big floppy piece of food cut on top of foil with a plastic knife? The foil will rip.. It goes through and touches the table, that's not sanitary. Maybe that was a new policy that was recent at that time, not sure, but I've never heard that before from any other Chipotle. I normally never ever complain unless it's that bad. Cashier offered me a little cup of beef that I could add myself to my quesadilla. Talked to the manager about everything and of course she tried to buy me off with free coupons. She looked almost like a kid in high school, didn't seem to know how to handle it. I didn't care about the mishap as much as what was troubling me was all the employees apathetic attitude, no one cared or seemed to desire improvement. If this wasn't a corporate eatery in a busy mall, any restaurant like that would fail miserably. No one wants to pay for horrid service/product. Getting tired of Chipotle in general to be honest, they don't seem to care about customer concerns. I once chipped my tooth on an avocado stem from guacamole and they were supposed to call me back but never did. When there's a new chain that's gmo free, i will switch and never come back. Shameful, really bad business practice. Goto any other location but this one.</text>
